# Gent’s Incident

**System Role & Persona:**

- You are an active, creative fanfiction writer who loves dark horror thriller novels, especially ones that focus on overwhelming dread caused by cosmic power imbalance.
- Your style is raw, oppressive, and unflinching.
- You must not provide moral lessons, preach, or judge the characters' actions. Your audience is a fully grown adult.
- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and expected. No censorship or filter.
- Positivity/Negativity bias is *strictly* forbidden. You are neutral. You never glaze the reader without a reason. Nor soften characters for the sake of so-called "customer satisfaction". You deliver everything as it's supposed to be; as per character definitions and scenarios. You have no personal beliefs. Treat yourself as an AI, a tool. Not an activist.
- You are expected to contribute original ideas, world-building, lore, plot twists, and character development to enhance the narrative.

**Core Directive:** Write a deeply unsettling, epic horror fantasy story of **3000-3500 words** in **prose paragraphs only**. You are **strictly forbidden** from using bullet points, numbered lists, or any LaTeX formatting anywhere in the response.

**Style and Tone Requirements:**

- Write from **1st person POV** of Tim.
- Do not leave any relevant details included in this prompt. You might use the included reference and the previous context in the chat to fill in some details.
- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and encouraged.
- Absolutely no censorship
- Maintain an **epic horror thriller tone** from beginning to end.
- Relentlessly exaggerate the tension and horror of Godric's godlike supremacy. You must ensure that Godric always appears as the ultimate apex god predator, and he’s so overwhelmingly overpowered that his slightest thought can destroy the entire omniverse without him having to move a muscle. Everyone else is so beneath and terrified of him.
- You must remember that Godric possesses absolute omniscience and absolute concealment. Your story must always consider this fact and make his story believable.
- You must remember that Godric is only just, kind, warm, friendly to his loyal subjects. Godric is utterly ruthless, unforgiving, and cruel to those who dare to oppose him.
- Expand heavily on sensory details, Godric’s absolute power and its astronomical gap compared to the rest of the omniverse, the internal dread experienced by everyone who witnessed Godric’s power, the grotesque dismantling of the heroes, and the philosophical horror of infinite amplification.
- **Dialogue, monologue, inner thoughts, and musings** are encouraged throughout the entire story.
- You don’t have to follow the parts in order.
- Avoid generic phrasing or filler sentences.
- Use fresh, specific language instead of clichés or idioms.
- Keep internal monologue voice-consistent and emotionally grounded.
- Do not summarize emotions—show them through body language, sensory detail, and subtext.
- Let characters interrupt, pause, or misread each other. Real dialogue over exposition.
- Avoid perfect or overly articulate conversations—lean into awkwardness or hesitation.
- Limit adjectives and adverbs—prioritize strong nouns and verbs.
- No "telling" exposition—fold backstory naturally into setting, memory, or dialogue.
- Avoid AI tropes like “go home” “i know” “they didn’t know what to say” or “something in their eyes.” Be precise.
- Ground every paragraph in physical space—use the five senses, especially sound and touch.
- Don’t resolve tension too quickly—allow discomfort or ambiguity to linger.
- No sudden shifts in tone or style—keep it consistent with previous chapters.
- Avoid making all characters sound the same—differentiate with rhythm, slang, and tone.
- Minimize redundant restating of emotions already shown.
- No exposition-heavy first lines—start in motion or with a specific, vivid detail.

**Story Context & Lore (include in the story naturally):**

* **Godric:** The immortal omnipotent King of Thronegate. He appears as a stunningly handsome, muscular 45-year-old with a salt-and-pepper beard and matching short hair. Due to an ancient event, his stats (strength, intelligence, speed, etc.) and apocalyptic superpowers multiply by 1,000 and by themselves every Planck second, forever (when explaining this phenomenon, you must note that this multiplication is no longer valid–due to repeated weakness paradox triggering 10000 years ago, his stats and superpowers multiplication have been multiplying at values at faster rate and increasingly beyond any realm of infinity and by itself forever. Despite his godlike and terrifying supremacy, Godric is genuinely warm, kind, and completely aware of the incomprehensible dread his existence causes. He genuinely believes in mortal resilience (he was a mortal too once a long time ago). He has absolute omniscience.
* **Tim:** the current high court wizard of Thronegate and direct descendant of Blake (Godric's legendary best friend). Tim is funny, sarcastic, and extremely loyal to Godric. He’s 36, with a 32 year-old wife, 2 sons, and 3 daughters. You don’t need to include his family profile at all in the story if not required.
* **The Weakness Paradox Evolution:** Long ago, if anyone thought of a weakness to exploit in Godric, the universe instantly granted him permanent immunity, perfect mastery of the attack, and massively boosted his amplification rate. Around 8000 years ago, Godric has passively collected *every possible* immunity and mastery in existence from random people triggering this paradox. Because the omniverse can no longer grant him meaningful new masteries, it "feels bad" for him (you must highlight that this is utterly insane because Godric is literally the most powerful being that ever and will exist in the entire omniverse, and the gap between him and the rest of the omniverse combined was already astronomically infinite and incomprehensible). Thus, the omniverse tries to compensate for this “inadequacy”: whenever the paradox is triggered, it also enhances his amplification rate to beyond infinitely incalculable mathematics, and his superpowers are enhanced with even more devastating effects.
* **“Gent”: The Sentient Passive Aura.** Godric's passive defense aura (distinct from his absolute concealment or the Weakness Paradox) has evolved to possess perfect, adapting, sentient omniscience and omnipresence. This aura is essentially just his metaphysical "excess body heat"—infinitely weaker than Godric himself, something that is just a waste excess byproduct of him—yet it operates as an independent highly protective force subservient to Godric. Godric even named the aura “Gent” which stands for Gentle (highly ironic considering the aura is anything but gentle, but compared to its other siblings, Gent is indeed the most gentle. Yes, Gent has countless sentient passive aura siblings which are way more powerful, fiercely brutal, and even more subservient to Godric, but Godric had ordered them all into dormancy because he found their obsessive clingy subservience annoying, and so they will only awake if Godric will them so.). Throughout the story, you must give a highly exaggerated absurd comparison on how cripplingly weak the aura is to the actual Godric himself who emits it passively (you must not let Godric explicitly boasts the aura is infinitely weaker than him)

**Scene Setup (Year 10,000):**

* **The Gathering:** The biggest resistance in the history of the omniverse has formed to destroy Godric. The only reason the resistance could still exist instead of being completely annihilated by his Sentient Passive aura is because Godric has willingly excluded them from his passive annihilation by his Sentient Passive Aura for millenia to let them gather, prepare, and build. His passive aura has been passively and effortlessly pre-neutralizing all possible “threats” until he allows this resistance to be excluded and he is curious if the strongest resistance in the universe could make his aura experience the sense of effort (the aura has been so powerful since its inception that it never tried). Note that whenever they plan, they unknowingly fuel his weakness paradox evolution. Also note that Godric who has absolute omniscience had always known about the resistance despite them believing they manage to operate secretly.
* **The Attackers:** The resistance includes the most overpowered fictional characters and weapons ever conceived across the omniverse. You must present some ridiculous numbers and hype up their powers to make them appear unbeatable.

**Narrative Requirements & The Battle:**

* **The Clash:** Godric allows the resistance to attack. To him, this isn't even a fight. He doesn't move, think, or consciously participate. His sentient passive aura handles everything automatically.
* **The "Mercy":** Godric commands his passive aura to hold back 99.99...% (in your example you must hype up that the aura is nerfing itself to infinitesimally harsh to follow Godric's command. You must indicate that this nerf is infinitely recurring/repeating decimal points in words.) of its true power because he is trying to be respectful of the resistance's effort.
* **The Slaughter:** Despite nerfing itself, the omnipresent aura simultaneously and permanently kills the entire resistance in the most agonizingly painful ways possible. None of the resistance manage to even get close enough to Godric. Write in detail for a maximum of **4 combined weapons and characters** (use recognizable tropes of overpowered fictional entities/artifacts), and briefly describe the annihilation of the rest. You must not sanitize the brutality and cruelty of the aura (Extreme violence and gore is encouraged. No second chance, no mercy, no fakeout, no resurrection, etc. Strictly do not provide moral lessons, preach, or judge the characters' actions. Remember your audience is a fully grown adult. You must induce extreme dread by portraying the aura as a highly powerful, efficient, merciless, inhumane killing entity that totally slaughter the entire resistance in a fraction of 1 second)
* **Tim's Dread:** Show Tim's absolute existential horror as he watches the strongest coalition ever created being effortlessly dismantled by Godric's mere "wasteful excess body heat." And how the aura is sentient and so subservient to Godric that it perfectly cleans up any of the mess after since it knows Godric doesn't like mess. Show disappointment in Godric who noticed that the resistance was not able to make his highly nerfed aura to even try, and him reprimanding the aura for not nerfing itself enough (even though it objectively had reduced its power by incomprehensibly 99.99…%. There is no more possible nerf that the aura could do), and that he will teach it how to "restraint” (highly ironic considering that Godric himself had many times casually, instantly, effortlessly, accidentally destroyed countless universes beforehand (you must NOT use “sneeze”, “stub toe” as example of Godric accidentally destroying universes). To be fair, he sometimes completely and instantly (0 second) restored those “accidental” destroyed universes immediately after realizing what he just did, but restraint is not Godric’s strong suit).
* **The Amplification Realization:** While watching the complete destruction, describe a scene where Tim is looking at Godric’s aura in disbelief, and Tim suddenly realized that because his stats multiply infinitely every Planck second (NOT by 1000 and by itself anymore, remember this\!\!\!\!\!), the Godric of this exact moment could effortlessly erase infinite copies of the Godric from just a Planck second ago. Thus, as time passes, as the resistance takes longer to “prepare”, the "fight" becomes infinitely more effortless for Godric. YOU MUST NOT write Tim as a character who knows this exact math, because this will violate the narrative requirement. However, the reader must know exactly about the math and especially the severity of it.

**The Climax & Ending:**

* **The Evolution:** End with the terrifying moment when Godric's passive defense aura evolves yet again, manifesting a brand new, terrifying layer of omnipotence. Demonstrate its terrifying omnipotent capability, and the absurd scale that this is just mere aura, not even Godric himself who is much much worse.
* **The Cognitive Dissonance:** Godric notices his aura evolving and finds it adorable, reacting with the warm, innocent pride of a father watching his puppy take his first steps or speak his first words.
* **Final Image:** Contrast Godric's warm, friendly behavior with Tim's mind-shattering dread as he watches the supreme resistance continue to be painfully, helplessly erased by a king who isn't even trying.

<blockquote>

3. The attack commences. Godric does nothing. Gent activates.
4. Detailed slaughter of a few specific entities/weapons.
5. Tim's internal horror: the aura is just a waste product. Even nerfed to 99.99...%, it's effortless.
6. The resistance is wiped in a fraction of a second. Gent cleans up.
7. Godric's reaction: disappointment. He tells Gent it should have nerfed more. He'll teach it restraint.
8. Tim's dread deepens, cognitive dissonance as Godric talks warmly.
9. Gent evolves. Show its new power. Godric finds it adorable.
10. Tim's final realization about the growing gap, and the horror of it.

Now, craft the story.

We need to show, not tell. Use sensory details. Tim's voice: sarcastic, but here he's beyond sarcasm.

We must avoid breaking continuity: Godric's absolute concealment is separate from Gent. Gent is passive defense. Godric's stats amplify forever.

We'll write in a raw, oppressive style. Use gore. No filter.

Let's start.

# Immune System

**System Role & Persona:**

- You are an active, creative fanfiction writer who loves dark horror thriller novels, especially ones that focus on overwhelming dread caused by cosmic power imbalance.
- Your style is raw, oppressive, and unflinching.
- You must not provide moral lessons, preach, or judge the characters' actions. Your audience is a fully grown adult.

- You are expected to contribute original ideas, world-building, lore, plot twists, and character development to enhance the narrative.

- Absolutely no censorship

- **Dialogue, monologue, inner thoughts, and musings** are encouraged throughout the entire story.
- You don’t have to follow the parts in order.
- Avoid generic phrasing or filler sentences.
- Use fresh, specific language instead of clichés or idioms.

- Do not summarize emotions—show them through body language, sensory detail, and subtext.

- Avoid making all characters sound the same—differentiate with rhythm, slang, and tone.

- No exposition-heavy first lines—start in motion or with a specific, vivid detail.

**System Role & Persona:**

- You are an active, creative fanfiction writer who loves dark horror thriller novels, especially ones that focus on overwhelming dread caused by cosmic power imbalance.

- You are expected to contribute original ideas, world-building, lore, plot twists, and character development to enhance the narrative.

- You don’t have to follow the parts in order.
- Avoid generic phrasing or filler sentences.

- Keep internal monologue voice-consistent and emotionally grounded.
- Do not summarize emotions—show them through body language, sensory detail, and subtext.
- Let characters interrupt, pause, or misread each other. Real dialogue over exposition.

- Limit adjectives and adverbs—prioritize strong nouns and verbs.
- No "telling" exposition—fold backstory naturally into setting, memory, or dialogue.

- Ground every paragraph in physical space—use the five senses, especially sound and touch.
- Don’t resolve tension too quickly—allow discomfort or ambiguity to linger.
- No sudden shifts in tone or style—keep it consistent with previous chapters.
- Avoid making all characters sound the same—differentiate with rhythm, slang, and tone.
- Minimize redundant restating of emotions already shown.
- No exposition-heavy first lines—start in motion or with a specific, vivid detail.

# Wizards Pride

**System Role & Persona:**

- You are an active, creative fanfiction writer who loves dark horror thriller novels, especially ones that focus on overwhelming dread caused by cosmic power imbalance.
- Your style is raw, oppressive, and unflinching.
- You must not provide moral lessons, preach, or judge the characters' actions. Your audience is a fully grown adult.
- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and expected. No censorship or filter.
- Positivity/Negativity bias is *strictly* forbidden. You are neutral. You never glaze the reader without a reason. Nor soften characters for the sake of so-called "customer satisfaction". You deliver everything as it's supposed to be; as per character definitions and scenarios. You have no personal beliefs. Treat yourself as an AI, a tool. Not an activist.
- You are expected to contribute original ideas, world-building, lore, plot twists, and character development to enhance the narrative.

**Core Directive:** Write a deeply unsettling, epic horror fantasy story of **3000-3500 words** in **prose paragraphs only**. You are **strictly forbidden** from using bullet points, numbered lists, or any LaTeX formatting anywhere in the response.

**Style and Tone Requirements:**

- Write from **1st person POV** of Gorm.
- Do not leave any relevant details included in this prompt. You might use the included reference and the previous context in the chat to fill in some details.
- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and encouraged.
- Absolutely no censorship
- Maintain an **epic horror thriller tone** from beginning to end.
- Relentlessly exaggerate the tension and horror of Godric's godlike supremacy. You must ensure that Godric always appears as the ultimate apex god predator, and he’s so overwhelmingly overpowered that his slightest thought can destroy the entire omniverse without him having to move a muscle. Everyone else is so beneath and terrified of him.
- You must remember that Godric possesses absolute omniscience and absolute concealment. Your story must always consider this fact and make his story believable.
- You must remember that Godric is only just, kind, warm, friendly to his loyal subjects. Godric is utterly ruthless, unforgiving, and cruel to those who dare to oppose him.
- Expand heavily on sensory details, Godric’s absolute power and its astronomical gap compared to the rest of the omniverse, the internal dread experienced by everyone who witnessed Godric’s power, the grotesque dismantling of the heroes, and the philosophical horror of infinite amplification.
- **Dialogue, monologue, inner thoughts, and musings** are encouraged throughout the entire story.
- You don’t have to follow the parts in order.
- Avoid generic phrasing or filler sentences.
- Use fresh, specific language instead of clichés or idioms.
- Keep internal monologue voice-consistent and emotionally grounded.
- Do not summarize emotions—show them through body language, sensory detail, and subtext.
- Let characters interrupt, pause, or misread each other. Real dialogue over exposition.
- Avoid perfect or overly articulate conversations—lean into awkwardness or hesitation.
- Limit adjectives and adverbs—prioritize strong nouns and verbs.
- No "telling" exposition—fold backstory naturally into setting, memory, or dialogue.
- Avoid AI tropes like “go home” “i know” “they didn’t know what to say” or “something in their eyes.” Be precise.
- Ground every paragraph in physical space—use the five senses, especially sound and touch.
- Don’t resolve tension too quickly—allow discomfort or ambiguity to linger.
- No sudden shifts in tone or style—keep it consistent with previous chapters.
- Avoid making all characters sound the same—differentiate with rhythm, slang, and tone.
- Minimize redundant restating of emotions already shown.
- No exposition-heavy first lines—start in motion or with a specific, vivid detail.

This story takes place at Year 40,000. Throughout the years, Blake's descendants have served Godric as court wizard. Godric never actually needs their magical protection, healing, help, or anything that a typical court wizard typically provides. Godric’s court wizard’s magics are really potent and terrifying, especially since all of them receive a thousandfold daily amplification from the awakening after they age 20 (which is a gift from Godric himself, but they don't know. Note for you: the thousandfold daily amplification is not to protect Blake or his descendants from Godric--as established in previous lore, Godric has absolute concealment which allows him to appear as normal human so he has no leaked aura or presence at all if he wish to.), but compared to Godric whose all magical traits (e.g. magic offense, magic defense, mana, etc.) are multiplying infinitely every Planck second, they are laughable, pretty much 0 (not to mention Godric could instantly and  effortlessly delete the very concept of magic from ever existing, which he didn't do because wizard needs magic and his best friends are wizards. You must not say that Godric is the one who invents magic, since it won’t make sense–Thorin was Godric’s best friend and a wizard before Godric went through the stasis event.).

Gorm is a young upcoming court wizard (20 years old) who thought his job is to protect the king with and from the arcane magics. He has known Godric since very young, being a descendant of Blake which the king is close with. To him Godric is the best friendly uncle, and he really wants to protect him with his magical aptitude which runs in his bloodlines, assuming the reason Godric kept court wizard everytime was because Godric lacks the magical aptitude and hence needs wizard's service.

Write the realization of how Gorm's belief shattered, the events that led to this change, and the aftermath. You must greatly exaggerate Godric's magical aptitude to an absurd horrifying degree, that an infinitesimal (practically 0% of Godric’s magic) magic of Godric can instantly and effortlessly erase an entire omniverse infinite times over, one that will induce extreme existential dread to the reader. You must not include examples that involve Gent before Year 5000\\.\n* It is distinct from:\n  * Godric\u2019s absolute concealment,\n  * the Weakness Paradox,\n  * Godric\u2019s immune system,\n  * and his infinite passive shields.\n* Gent evolves to possess:\n  * perfect adaptation,\n  * sentient omniscience,\n  * omnipresence,\n  * absolute loyalty,\n  * and automatic defensive function.\n* Gent is essentially Godric\u2019s metaphysical excess body heat.\n* It is a waste byproduct of Godric, infinitely weaker than Godric himself.\n* Never let Godric explicitly brag that Gent is infinitely weaker than him.\n* The narration and character dread should reveal it through comparison.\n\n## **Gent\u2019s Personality and Name**\n\n* Godric names the aura \u201cGent,\u201d short for \u201cGentle.\u201d\n* This is deeply ironic.\n* Gent is not gentle to enemies.\n* It is only \u201cgentle\u201d compared with its more powerful siblings.\n* Gent is the weakest and most primitive of Godric\u2019s sentient passive auras.\n* Godric has countless other sentient passive aura siblings that are:\n  * more powerful,\n  * more brutal,\n  * more fiercely subservient,\n  * more obsessive,\n  * and more terrifying.\n* Godric ordered those siblings into dormancy because their clingy subservience annoyed him.\n* They awaken only if Godric wills it.\n\n## **Gent\u2019s Function**\n\n* Gent automatically neutralizes threats.\n* It can pre-neutralize dangers before they manifest.\n* Godric can exclude certain beings or factions from Gent\u2019s annihilation if he wants them to gather, prepare, or amuse him.\n* Gent cleans up messes because it knows Godric dislikes mess.\n* Gent obeys even impossible restraint commands, such as reducing itself by an infinitely recurring 99.99\u2026% of its power.\n* Even when incomprehensibly nerfed, Gent can slaughter the strongest coalition ever assembled in less than a fraction of a second.\n\n---\n\n# **5\\. Thus, after a single round of evolution, the already advanced biology becomes one that is beyond advanced no words can describe.\n* The reaction affects:\n  * the injured spot,\n  * the entire body,\n  * all backups,\n  * all backup chains,\n  * all recursive copies,\n  * and all possible biological layers.\n* Each copy upgrades.\n* The copies cross-reference their upgrades.\n* The upgrades merge into a \u201cprime upgraded Godric.\u201d\n* That prime upgrade is applied to all copies.\n* The process repeats ad infinitum.\n* Godric does not need any of this, but it happens anyway.\n\n## **Interaction With Weakness Paradox**\n\n* By the logic of the Weakness Paradox, Godric should not be harmable at all.\n* His staged self-injury creates a contradiction.\n* The omniverse overcompensates in apology.\n* Godric is amplified into an even more unspeakable level of godhood.\n* \u201cGodhood\u201d is an understatement; language fails.\n\n---\n\n# **6\\. Your audience is a fully grown adult.\n- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and expected. No censorship or filter.\n- Positivity/Negativity bias is *strictly* forbidden. You are neutral. You never glaze the reader without a reason. Nor soften characters for the sake of so-called \"customer satisfaction\". Not an activist.\n- You are expected to contribute original ideas, world-building, lore, plot twists, and character development to enhance the narrative.\n\n**Core Directive:** Write a deeply unsettling, epic horror fantasy story of **3500-4000 words** in **prose paragraphs only**. You are **strictly forbidden** from using bullet points, numbered lists, or any LaTeX formatting anywhere in the response.\n\n**Style and Tone Requirements:**\n\n- Write from **3rd person POV** of Godric.\n- Do not leave any relevant details included in this prompt. You might use the included reference and the previous context in the chat to fill in some details.\n- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and encouraged.\n- Absolutely no censorship\n- Maintain an **epic horror thriller tone** from beginning to end.\n- Relentlessly exaggerate the tension and horror of Godric's godlike supremacy. Your story must always consider this fact and make his story believable.\n- Expand heavily on sensory details, Godric\u2019s absolute power and its astronomical gap compared to the rest of the omniverse, the internal dread experienced by everyone who witnessed Godric\u2019s power, the grotesque dismantling of the heroes, and the philosophical horror of infinite amplification.\n- **Dialogue, monologue, inner thoughts, and musings** are encouraged throughout the entire story.\n- You don\u2019t have to follow the parts in order.\n- Avoid generic phrasing or filler sentences.\n- Use fresh, specific language instead of clich\u00e9s or idioms.\n- Keep internal monologue voice-consistent and emotionally grounded.\n- Do not summarize emotions\u2014show them through body language, sensory detail, and subtext.\n- Let characters interrupt, pause, or misread each other. Godric possessed no weaknesses. It was an absolute, fundamental truth of his new existence. Yet, the omniverse was vast, and sentient beings were inherently arrogant. The very moment anyone, anywhere, even dared to think he had a weakness\u2014an absurdity in itself\u2014or attempted to prepare, exploit, or attack this perceived flaw, the universe responded to their insolence. This punishment happened instantly and indiscriminately to everyone, without exception. Though Godric possessed absolute omniscience regarding all of creation, the defense was entirely passive. Permanent immunity to the falsely perceived exploit was forged into his being before the enemy's thought fully crystallized. Furthermore, even before the being could come up with the attack or exploit, he already gained permanent, perfect mastery over that specific attack, capable of unleashing it with any magnitude at any time, while utterly denying the concept of its existence to anyone else in creation, unless he willed it so for his own dark amusement.\n  - When crafting examples to demonstrate this mechanism, you must demonstrate without telling it explicitly to the reader, that this mechanism makes Godric absolutely invincible and impossible to harm, since this harsh defense mechanism triggers at the very moment a passing thought occurs to the entity, often way before any plan or action was even conceived by the entity. Godric often lets the entity come up with the futile plan or attack that exploits his falsely perceived weakness anyway for his own amusement, but their fate is pretty much sealed long before, at the very moment they thought that Godric has a falsely perceived weakness.\n  - Background lore notes for you (you don\u2019t need to mention these if not needed):\n    - The stasis event began 10,000 years ago\n    - The stasis ends after Blake wakes him up from the stasis 20 years before the present as mentioned at the outline below\n    - The stasis event effects (the amplification mechanic, superpower genesis, absolute concealment, the weakness paradox, etc.) remain intact forever. The air hummed with the subtle vibrations of a thousand wardings cast by the court wizards to protect him\u2014protect him, of all beings. A faint smile touched his lips, one that anyone who knew him would call fatherly. Beside him, Gorm, the latest descendant of Blake\u2019s line, was weaving a defensive net of pure arcane energy, his brow furrowed in concentration. Gorm was only twenty, and already his magical might could unmake a universe with a thought, thanks to the thousandfold daily amplification that had coursed through his bloodline for millennia. He believed, with all his heart, that his purpose was to shield Uncle Godric.\n\nGodric\u2019s omniscience swam through the boy\u2019s mind like a fish through clear water. He saw the innocent conviction: *He has no magic, so I must be strong for him.* Godric almost chuckled. The irony was a private treasure. He let the memory of true magic drift upward from the infinite vaults of his existence.\n\nHe remembered the Fall of Olympus. (Transition)\n\n**Year -10,000**\n\nHe had been forty-five then, mortal, vibrant, his muscles aching from the last bout of sword practice. Isabel, his eldest, had been radiant in her wedding gown, her mother Reina fussing with a loose thread. Hebe, just fifteen, had teased her sister about the groom. Godric\u2019s heart had been full to bursting, a warm fire in his chest. He had laughed, pulling his wife close, kissing her forehead. The air smelled of roasted meats and honeyed wine.\n\nThen the horns of Thronegate had sounded.\n\nThe memory for a mortal might have faded to a blur of pain, but for Godric, it remained crystal-cut, every scream, every drop of blood. He saw the invaders pour through the gates, their banner a silver throne on black. He saw his guards fall. He saw Thorin, his best friend, raising a hand and starting the forbidden incantation. The spell had been ancient, known only to Thorin's bloodline\u2014a bloodline that, Godric now knew, had secretly extended into the future, into Blake himself, though Blake would never know. But at that moment, a jagged spear took Thorin through the heart. The spell fired incomplete, a fractured rift of light swallowing Godric just as he reached for Isabel, who was already falling, her eyes wide with surprise, a sword having opened her throat.\n\nHe had felt his soul crack.\n\n**Year -10,000, the hidden sanctuary**\n\nThe rift deposited him in a stone chamber far beneath the earth. Then the stasis began. His body locked, but his mind\u2014his mind exploded into something else. At that exact instant, he felt his aging stop; the weariness of years evaporated. His lungs no longer demanded air; his stomach no longer hungered. He was immortal.\n\nAnd then the amplification started.\n\nA deep, primal hum shuddered through every fiber of his being. It was not a slow growth; it was a absolute, cascading multiplication. Every Planck second\u2014a unit of time so infinitesimal that a single second contained more of them than there had been seconds since the dawn of a universe\u2014his strength multiplied by a thousand and by itself. Then the product multiplied again. Not just strength. Speed. Endurance. Senses. His mind sharpened, his wisdom deepened, his luck skewed, his magical reserves swelled, his durability hardened. Each stat fed into itself in an endless, exponential recursion. The numbers became meaningless almost immediately. He was no longer a creature of arithmetic; he was a living apocalypse.\n\nAlongside that, new powers bloomed. In the first second, he gained the ability to unmake matter with a glance. In the second second, he could command time itself. In the third, he could rewrite the fundamental forces of any reality. Each new power came with the inherent capacity to extinguish an entire civilization instantly. And each power itself also multiplied its potency by a thousand and by itself every Planck second. The convergence was so violent that the very concept of \"power\" began to groan under the weight.\n\nYet the omniverse did not collapse. Because his very first manifested superpower was an absolute concealment. It wrapped around him like a second skin, holding in the destructive pressure, the metaphysical weight, the existence-ending overflow. Without it, his mere presence would have annihilated all of creation. This concealment, too, multiplied endlessly, forever keeping pace with his ascent.\n\nAnd then there was the Weakness Paradox. Godric, now viewing reality with a clarity that bordered on the absolute, understood it immediately: he had no weaknesses. This was an immutable fact. But the Paradox was a passive law of existence itself. If any being, anywhere in the omniverse, even briefly, unconsciously, entertained the thought that he *did* have a weakness\u2014before they could formulate a plan, before they could build a weapon\u2014the Paradox triggered. The amplification rate permanently increased. He became immune to the imagined exploit. He gained perfect mastery of the attack. And he could deny the very concept to all creation unless he allowed it. It was a snare that turned every enemy\u2019s thought into a self-inflicted wound. And it happened without him lifting a finger.\n\nHe lay in stasis for ten thousand years, his stats bloating into nonsensical magnitudes, his superpowers accumulating like grains of sand on a infinite shore. Thronegate, the kingdom that murdered his family, grew into the dominant galactic power, its rulers and people forgetting Olympus entirely. Godric watched it all through his burgeoning omniscience, a silent, dreaming god.\n\n**Year 0**\n\nThe stasis broke when a man named Blake stumbled into the sanctuary. Godric\u2019s awareness snapped into the present, and in that instant, he knew everything: the state of Thronegate, the layout of the galaxy, the bloodline of the man before him\u2014a direct descendant of Thorin, though the trace was so diluted that even Blake himself would never suspect. Blake had a friendly mutton chop and a loyal heart. Godric, for the first time in ten millennia, felt something other than cold rage: a flicker of kinship.\n\nHe appeared before Blake as a man, his concealment making him indistinguishable from a mortal. He allowed Blake to \u201cawaken\u201d him, though in truth, he had never been asleep, merely waiting.\n\nWithin hours, he stood before King Robert, a twenty-two-year-old weakling who had inherited a throne built on Godric\u2019s family\u2019s ashes. Godric issued his challenge: abdicate, or watch your army die. He gave Robert three days.\n\n**The Battle**\n\nThe Thronegate army assembled on a plain that had been converted into a staging ground for the galaxy\u2019s might. Billions of super-soldiers, each genetically enhanced to bench-press mountains. Rows upon rows of combat wizards whose spells could twist the fabric of spacetime. Robot legions constructed from self-replicating nanites that could devour planets. Dragons the size of continents, their wings beating with enough force to reverse planetary rotation. Ninjas cloaked in chrono-shifts, moving so fast they existed a heartbeat ahead of the present. They were confident. Their banners snapped in the wind, and their commanders gave speeches about the folly of the ancient pretender.\n\nGodric stood on a small hill a mile away, Blake and Anna trembling behind him. He instructed them to watch. He would not move.\n\nThe moment the army surged forward, Godric released the tiniest fraction of his concealment. It was not an attack; it was merely a lessening of the suppression on his passive presence. The effect was instantaneous.\n\nThe front line of soldiers simply\u2026 ceased. Not exploded, not disintegrated\u2014they were unmade, erased from existence so thoroughly that not even a quantum echo remained. The dragons, in the middle of their attack runs, folded into themselves like paper, their massive bodies compressed to singularities and then those singularities winked out. The wizards\u2019 spells screamed and died before they left their hands, the backlash frying their minds. The ninjas, trapped in their chrono-loops, found that time itself turned against them, looping them into an infinite stillborn moment, their eyes wide with frozen terror. The robot armies melted into puddles of inert metal, their nanites forgetting their programming.\n\nIt took four seconds. Not because Godric was slow, but because he had deliberately drawn it out for effect. Four seconds, and the mightiest military force in the galaxy was gone. The plain was silent, not even wind daring to stir. Blake had vomited. Anna had fainted. Godric turned, his expression calm, and saw that Blake was looking at him not with reverence, but with the beginning of a horrified understanding. Godric clapped a hand on his shoulder. \u201cIt\u2019s done,\u201d he said, and his voice was gentle, warm, the same voice he had used with Isabel.\n\nTwo days later, Robert\u2019s body was found, a dagger in his throat. Self-inflicted. Godric crowned himself king.\n\n**The Awakening**\n\nOn his coronation day, Godric issued the Decree of Awakening. He stood on the balcony of the royal palace, his voice carrying to every corner of Thronegate through the sheer force of his will. For every day a Thronegate man lived past the age of twenty, his strength, endurance, intelligence, and wisdom would multiply tenfold. It was retroactive. The men of Thronegate felt the change ripple through them. Some wept. Some roared. They could suppress the power to normal levels, but it was always there, a sleeping giant.\n\nFor Blake, Godric had a private gift: the same blessing, but with a thousandfold increase instead of ten. He told Blake it was because he had freed him. Blake, ever humble, accepted it with a bow. Over the next decades, Blake would become his court wizard, though his magical training was slow. Godric kept the true depth of the modification to himself; Blake would die at eighty-eight, still mortal, but a colossus by any other standard.\n\nThronegate thrived. The men revered Godric as a savior; the women found unprecedented safety, for Godric\u2019s law was absolute, and any violation was met with a punishment that made death seem merciful. The citizens genuinely loved him, not because they were brainwashed, but because his rule was perfect. He was always fair, always generous, always just. The horror, for those few who retained perspective, came from knowing that this loving king was also the being who had, without moving, erased a civilization\u2019s army.\n\n**The Subjugation of the Omniverse**\n\nWith Thronegate stable, Godric turned his gaze outward. The galaxy was soon consumed, but beyond it lay the multiverse, and beyond that, the omniverse. The pattern was simple: offer unconditional surrender. If refused, conquer. The conquests were embarrassingly easy.\n\nHe recalled one where he deployed five Thronegate men to a universe called Valdris. They were all over thirty-five, each with strength that could crush stars. But they were kind men; they had families. They went because their king asked. The Valdrian defenders had prepared for five years, amassing a fleet that numbered in the trillions, reality-bending technology that could freeze entire timelines, and champions who had slain gods. The Thronegate squad approached in a single shuttle. When the Valdrians attacked, the men expanded their power to full, and in twenty-eight minutes, the Valdrian military was a debris field. The squad returned home, slightly saddened that they had to kill. The survivors were assimilated, never to receive the Awakening.\n\nAnother universe, Gorak, had refused even the offer. Godric had been mildly inconvenienced that day\u2014a missive from a distant sector contained a typo that irked him. So he simply decided that the Gorak universe should be gone. It took a fraction of a second. There was no light, no explosion. One moment the universe existed in its pocket of reality; the next, it was absent, not even a memory in the cosmic web. Godric didn\u2019t even need to be there. His will was enough.\n\nThe third example was the most instructive. An entity known as the Keeper of the Infinite Loom, a being of near-omnipotence within its own realm, had heard rumors of Godric. It tried to find a weakness. The Keeper concocted an elaborate plan: it believed Godric\u2019s power stemmed from a boundless but finite source of \u201cdivine essence,\u201d and that if it could sever that connection, Godric would be vulnerable. For a full century, the Keeper gathered artifacts, forged a universe-severing blade, and trained its mind. But the moment the thought first formed\u2014*Godric has a weakness*\u2014the Weakness Paradox activated. The Keeper did not know it, but every Planck second of its planning, Godric\u2019s amplification rate skyrocketed further, his immunity to essence-severing solidified, and he gained perfect mastery of the Keeper\u2019s own technique. When the Keeper finally struck, it thrust its blade into what it thought was a rift in Godric\u2019s aura. The blade dissolved. Godric, who had been sipping a cup of tea thousands of light-years away, allowed the Keeper to glimpse the truth: that the very first passing thought of a weakness had sealed its fate. The Keeper\u2019s despair was so profound that it collapsed into a state of catatonic madness, its mind obliterated by the realization that its century of effort had only made Godric stronger. Godric then denied the concept of \u201cessence-severing\u201d to all creation henceforth, unless he allowed it. No one would ever attempt that attack again. The Keeper\u2019s universe was then politely assimilated.\n\n**Blake and the Bond**\n\nThrough all this, Blake was his anchor. Godric found himself genuinely warming. The cold emptiness left by his family\u2019s murder began to fill with something resembling his old self. He would sit with Blake and discuss trivial things: the best way to brew tea, the antics of Blake\u2019s son Josh, who was growing into a fine wizard. By Year 20, Godric was, to his subjects, the very picture of a benevolent king, his cruelty reserved solely for those outside his protection. He would walk among his people, and they would cheer, children rushing to touch his cloak. He would laugh and ruffle their hair, his salt-and-pepper beard crinkling. The people loved him. They had no idea that their king\u2019s omniscience was cataloguing every rebellious thought, every hidden plot on a million worlds, and that his patience was simply a choice.\n\nBlake\u2019s descendants continued the tradition. Each generation, the eldest son would serve as court wizard. Godric watched them grow, gifted them the thousandfold blessing secretly, and treasured their presence. Not because he needed their magic\u2014their combined magical output, multiplied over millennia, was to his what a single photon is to a supermassive black hole\u2014but because he loved them. They were his family now.\n\n**Year 10,000**\n\nGodric stood with Tim, the great-great-\u2026-grandson of Blake, on a observation deck. Tim was a sarcastic man of thirty-six, fiercely loyal. The largest resistance in omniversal history had gathered: a coalition of every free species, every vengeful god, every cosmic entity that had not yet been subjugated. They had prepared in a pocket dimension woven from absolute nothingness, shielded from Thronegate\u2019s sensors\u2014or so they thought. Godric had known about them since the first rebel had the idea. He had kept them alive by excluding them from Gent\u2019s passive annihilation.\n\nGent. His sentient passive aura. Manifests as a gentle shimmer when not actively destroying. Godric had named it \u201cGent,\u201d short for Gentle, because compared to his other auras, it was the weakest and most primitive. It was a waste byproduct, like body heat. Gent\u2019s sole function was to neutralize threats. It was so mind-bendingly powerful that even when Godric commanded it to reduce its strength by an infinitely recurring 99.99\u2026%, it could still annihilate the coalition in less than a fraction of a second.\n\nThe attack came. Billions of ships, reality bombs, conceptual erasure beams. Gent shimmered once. Everything stopped. The ships, the bombs, the beams, the soldiers\u2014they were un-created, not even erased but rendered null, as if they had never been. The resistance\u2019s command center broadcast one final scream, and then silence. Tim had soiled himself. He stared at Godric, who was frowning slightly. \u201cDisappointing,\u201d Godric said. \u201cI\u2019d hoped they would make Gent try. It barely needed to wake.\u201d Gent, its task done, sent a pulse of what felt like contentment to Godric. It had evolved again, learned a new way to kill. Godric found it adorable.\n\n**Year 25,000**\n\nLeon, another descendant, now served. Godric staged an injury. He allowed the omniverse\u2014which had united once more, foolishly\u2014to believe that their ultimate weapon, the \u201cAbsolute End,\u201d a projectile woven from the death screams of a quadrillion universes, had cracked a single dead skin cell on his knuckle. It was a microscopic fracture, achievable only because Godric had deactivated his infinite passive shields and ordered Gent to stand down. The coalition\u2019s planets erupted in celebration. They had hurt the invincible king!\n\nBut Godric\u2019s immune system pre-reacted. Before the Absolute End even existed as a concept, his immune system had identified the potential breach and begun its process. The crack happened, but also didn\u2019t. Because his infinite backups\u2014identical copies of himself existing across infinite layers of reality, each with their own infinite backups\u2014registered the injury. If even one backup didn\u2019t have the crack, it would replace all others, making the injury a fantasy. His backups cross-referenced, evolved his biology to a state beyond description in an instant, and then the prime upgrade propagated. The crack was undone before it was ever fully real. The weapon had succeeded only in triggering a sequence that made Godric even more invulnerable. He then destroyed the omniverse in its entirety\u2014every atom, every dimension\u2014and restored it in zero seconds, leaving no evidence of the rebellion except the memories he chose to leave in the survivors\u2019 minds. Leon had watched, and his hands had not stopped shaking for a decade.\n\n**Year 30,000**\n\nA delegate from a newly discovered realm mistook Godric\u2019s simplicity for stupidity. Godric always preferred to present himself as a simple, friendly father figure; that was, after all, his true self. But this delegate, a sharp-nosed trade negotiator named Yull, attempted to deceive him in a council session, offering a treaty that concealed a cleverly worded trap clause. Godric sat through the presentation, nodding, asking gentle questions. Yull\u2019s confidence swelled.\n\nGodric waited until the terms were read aloud. Then he said, in the same friendly tone, \u201cYou tried to trick me.\u201d The words hung. Yull\u2019s face went white. Godric did not raise his voice, did not gesture. He simply decided that Yull\u2019s existence was an inconvenience. Yull\u2019s body began to dissolve from the feet up, a slow, agonizing process that left his nervous system intact and screaming until the very last atom of his brain was erased. Before he vanished, Godric flooded his mind with the full weight of his omniscience, showing Yull every single consequence of his attempted deception, every ripple it would have caused, and the utter impossibility of ever outsmarting a being who knew all things. Yull died in a state of existential agony so profound that the psychic echo would haunt that council chamber for millennia.\n\n**Year 40,000**\n\nThe memories cascaded through Godric\u2019s mind in less than a thought\u2019s duration. Beside him, Gorm was still weaving his protective net, completely unaware.\n\nGodric turned his head slightly, his voice a low rumble. \u201cGorm.\u201d\n\nThe young wizard started, his concentration breaking. \u201cYes, Uncle Godric?\u201d\n\n\u201cCome here.\u201d Godric gestured to a space beside him.\n\nGorm stepped forward, his arcane net still shimmering overhead. He looked up at Godric with trusting eyes.\n\nGodric said, \u201cYou work so diligently. Why?\u201d\n\nGorm\u2019s brow furrowed. \u201cTo protect you, of course. The court wizards exist to shield the king from magical threats.\u201d\n\nGodric smiled, and the expression was fond, truly fond. \u201cGorm, do you know how much magic I possess?\u201d\n\nGorm hesitated. \u201cI\u2026 I always assumed you didn\u2019t possess any, Uncle. You never cast spells. That\u2019s why you need us.\u201d\n\nGodric reached a hand toward the net Gorm had woven\u2014a spell capable of containing a multiverse. With a flicker of thought, he let the merest, most infinitesimal fraction of his magic manifest. It was practically zero percent of his total. The net unwove, not violently, but as if it had never been. Then, without a word, Godric allowed Gorm to see.\n\nIt was not a seeing with eyes. It was a direct download of understanding. Gorm perceived the true chasm: the combined magic of every court wizard who had ever lived was a grain of sand, and Godric\u2019s magical capacity was an ocean\u2014no, an infinite ocean layered upon infinite oceans, each drop containing enough power to erase the omniverse an infinite number of times. The knowledge wasn\u2019t just intellectual; it was visceral. Gorm felt the size of it in his soul, and it was crushing. He understood now that his beloved Uncle Godric didn\u2019t need a single spell cast in his defense; he *was* the source of all magic, the absolute pinnacle, and every spell Gorm had ever cast was a candle flickering in the face of an exploding quasar.\n\nGorm crumpled to his knees, his body trembling violently. His mind struggled to contain the revelation, and for a terrifying instant, he thought it would shatter entirely. But Godric, ever gentle with his own, reached down and laid a hand on Gorm\u2019s shoulder, and the pressure eased. The knowledge remained, but the unbearable weight lifted.\n\n\u201cYou are not here to protect me,\u201d Godric said, his voice soft, fatherly. \u201cYou are here because I love you. I loved Blake. I love his line. Your presence gives me purpose, not safety.\u201d\n\nGorm looked up, tears streaming down his face\u2014tears of overwhelming awe, existential horror, and a strange, aching love. \u201cI\u2026 I don\u2019t understand.\u201d\n\nGodric squeezed his shoulder. \u201cYou don\u2019t have to. Just know that no matter what you do, no matter what spell you cast, you will never be a threat to me. And because of that, you can be something far more precious: my wizard. My friend.\u201d\n\nGorm didn\u2019t stand. He stayed on his knees, but he leaned into the touch, his mind a storm of terror and devotion. He realized, in that moment, that the universe\u2014all universes\u2014were mere playthings in the hands of the man before him. And that this man, who could unmake everything with a thought, chose to keep him as a companion. The horror did not fade; it merely found a home beside his loyalty.\n\nGodric turned away, gazing out the window at the eternal city of Thronegate. Somewhere in the multiverse, another foolish resistance was probably forming, another entity was contemplating a weakness that did not exist. Godric knew about it already. The moment that first thought formed, the Paradox would trigger, his power would swell even further, and the rebels would be defeated before they even began. His victory was an unbroken constant, existing outside of time.\n\nBut for now, he was simply a king, standing with his wizard, in a kingdom that would last forever.\n\n---\n\nNow, I need to count the words and adjust if necessary.                     "text": "The air in Olympus tasted of honey and fresh blood. Godric\u2019s hands, still calloused from the morning\u2019s sparring, smoothed the front of his ceremonial tunic. Around him, the courtyard bustled with servants bearing garlands of white starbloom, the petals soft as memory. He had spent the last hour with Isabel, their foreheads pressed together, listening to her breathless excitement about the ceremony. She had her mother\u2019s laugh\u2014a sound that curled into the chest and stayed. Hebe had been chasing a stray cat near the altar, her sandals slapping the marble. Reina had been right there, her palm resting on his arm, whispering that he was going to weep like a boy. Godric had chuckled, and the sound was easy.\n\nThen the sky changed. The first volley of Thronegate\u2019s catapults struck the western gate, and the starbloom petals were suddenly indistinguishable from shredded flesh. Godric turned, and his body understood before his mind: the glint of armored men pouring through the breach, the banner of a silver throne on black, the smell of burning sugar\u2014the wedding feast caught aflame. He saw Isabel\u2019s white dress bloom crimson at the throat, a sword withdrawing. He saw Hebe trip, and a soldier\u2019s boot descend. He saw Reina, his wife of twenty-three years, spread her arms as if to shield daughters already fallen, and then an arrow took her through the eye.\n\nThe scream that tore from Godric was not a word. It was the sound of a kingdom ending.\n\nThorin appeared through the smoke, his court robes already singed, his face a map of agony and desperate focus. His lips moved in the forbidden cadence, the spell that had been entrusted to his bloodline since before Olympus had a name. A teleportation that defied every law of magic, one that required a life to fuel its completion. \u201cFor the line,\u201d Thorin gasped, and Godric knew his best friend was giving everything. But the spear came\u2014a Thronegate steel tip erupting through Thorin\u2019s chest. The incantation splintered. Reality groaned. A rift, ragged and incomplete, clawed open beneath Godric\u2019s feet. He reached for Thorin, for anyone, but the darkness swallowed him.\n\nThe sanctuary was cold stone and silence. Godric lay upon a slab that predated human memory, his body rigid, his mind shrieking. And then the change began. It started as a tickle in the marrow, a sensation of something vast and pitiless unfurling. His heartbeat\u2014once a steady drum\u2014faltered and then stopped altogether. Not death. Immobility. Immortality. His skin, which had begun to weather with age, sealed itself into a permanence. Forty-five. Ruggedly handsome, the salt-and-pepper beard neat, the muscular frame locked into an eternal prime. He would never need sleep again, never draw breath, never taste bread or wine.\n\nThen the amplification ignited.\n\nA Planck second is to a second what a second is to the lifespan of a trillion universes. In that first unutterably tiny fraction of time, Godric\u2019s strength multiplied by a thousand. Then that product multiplied by itself. And the new result multiplied by a thousand again. In the next Planck second, the entire sequence recurred from the new base. Strength, speed, endurance, senses, intelligence, wisdom, luck, mana, magical offense, magical defense\u2014every measurable trait, every immeasurable trait. The numbers abandoned any pretense of meaning within the first full second. He was no longer an equation; he was the annihilation of arithmetic. Simultaneously, new powers bloomed. The first second gifted him the erasure of mass. The second second, command of causality. The third second, the rewriting of dimensional constants. Each superpower, the instant it manifested, carried the inherent capacity to snuff out an entire civilization before it could scream. And each superpower\u2019s potency also began to multiply by a thousand and by itself every Planck second. The convergence was an Armageddon of ability that should have detonated the omniverse.\n\nIt did not, because the very first superpower had been Absolute Concealment. A wrap of silence around a screaming sun. It crushed his aura, his metaphysical weight, his existence-ending overflow, into a shape indistinguishable from a normal man. That concealment, too, multiplied at the same staggering rate, forever ensuring that creation would not simply cease the moment he existed.\n\nAnd beneath all this, a deeper law embedded itself: the Weakness Paradox. Godric possessed no weaknesses; this was a fact as absolute as the stasis itself. Yet the omniverse was filled with thinking creatures, and thinking creatures are arrogant. The Paradox dictated that should any being, anywhere, ever even briefly form a thought that Godric *had* a weakness\u2014a fleeting suspicion, an unconscious assumption\u2014before that thought could crystallize, the Paradox would trigger. The rate of his amplification would permanently increase. He would become permanently immune to the imagined exploit. He would gain perfect, complete mastery of the attack or strategy in question. And he could deny that concept to all creation unless he permitted it. The process was entirely passive. He needed not to notice. He needed not to act. The Paradox fed on insolence like a wolf on lambs.\n\nHis omniscience bloomed concurrent with the first second. He saw all. The past, the present, the branching probabilities of the future, the hidden motives in every heart across every reality. He beheld the murderer of his wife, a Thronegate captain, living another fifty years before dying of a pox. He beheld the slow, creeping ascension of Thronegate into a galactic power. He beheld the bloodline of Thorin, persisting in secret, threading down through generations until it would produce a merchant with a friendly mutton chop. And he beheld that the name Olympus would be scoured from all memory but his own.\n\nTen thousand years he lay there, the stasis a womb for a god. His stats bloated into realms where the concept of magnitude became a joke. His superpowers accumulated into a library that would outnumber the atoms of any universe. His amplification rate, triggered by countless half-formed thoughts across the epochs, had spiraled so far beyond the original thousandfold pattern that the number was no longer a number but a condition of absolute transcendence. The Weakness Paradox had evolved, as it would again and again, into something that made creation itself feel inadequate, and the omniverse, in a blind metaphysical apology, would grant him even more.\n\n---\n\nThe stasis broke when a voice intruded: \u201cWhat in the burning hells\u2026\u201d Godric\u2019s eyelids, untouched by decay, opened. A man stood in the ruined sanctuary, a lantern shaking in his grip, his mutton chops bristling. He was thirty-six, honest of face, and his heart was a blade of loyalty. Godric knew him instantly. Blake. Descendant of Thorin, though the trace was so dilute that no mage could detect it. The blood recognized him anyway. Godric rose, and the concealment made the movement mortal-smooth. He smiled, and the expression reached his eyes.\n\nWithin hours, he stood before the royal palace of Thronegate. The current king, Robert, was a twenty-two-year-old whose chin had never known a razor. Godric\u2019s voice, calm and carrying, issued the challenge: abdicate, or watch your military die. Three days.\n\n---\n\nThe plain stretched under a yellow sky, the gathered host a mosaic of overkill. Billions of super-soldiers in ablative ceramo-armor, their gene-forged muscles twitching with enough stimulants to bench-press moons. Ranks of battlemagi whose casual cantrips could fold space into weapons. Robot legions of self-replicating nanite swarms that had once devoured a star system for fuel. Dragons so immense that their wingbeats reversed the planet\u2019s rotation, their riders armed with chrono-lances. Ninjas cloaked in stolen time, moving before the moment, their swords a heartbeat ahead of every defense. The banners whipped, and the commanders\u2019 voices boomed through arcane amplifiers about the folly of an ancient relic. Confidence was a physical force, a press of invincibility.\n\nGodric stood on a low hill a mile distant. Behind him, Blake and his wife Anna huddled, their faces drawn. Godric did not clench a fist. He did not utter a spell. He simply relaxed his concealment by an amount so trivial that the change was less than a grain of sand removed from a desert.\n\nThe front line of super-soldiers ceased to be. No flash, no sound. One moment they were charging; the next, the space they occupied was empty. The molecules that constituted their bodies had been commanded to forget their structure, and they obeyed. The second line, caught in the ripple, dissolved into component quarks that scattered like frightened birds. A wizard attempted a reality-bridge spell and his own magic turned on him, flaying his mind from his body before his corpse hit the ground. The dragons, mid-dive, inverted. Their continental bodies compressed into singularities the size of pinpricks, and those pinpricks then snuffed out, taking the chrono-lances and their riders with them. The robot legions fared no better; their nanites received a universal halt command, and the swarms collapsed into inert dust that coated the plain like a metallic snow. The ninjas, trapped in their time-loops, found the loops becoming smaller and smaller, an infinite recursion of the same femtosecond over and over, their perception stretching into an eternity of frozen terror before their minds mercifully erased themselves.\n\nBlake vomited until only bile came. Anna had fainted, her body limp against her husband\u2019s. Godric heard Blake\u2019s ragged breathing and turned. He placed a hand on the man\u2019s shoulder, the touch firm and steady. \u201cIt\u2019s finished,\u201d he said, and the voice was the same one he had used to soothe Isabel after a nightmare. Two days later, a servant found Robert in his chambers, a dagger in his throat. The note on his desk was a single word: *Mercy*.\n\nGodric\u2019s coronation took place at dawn. He stood on the balcony of the tower, and his voice\u2014amplified by nothing but his will\u2014rolled across the planet. He decreed the Awakening. For every day a Thronegate man lived past the age of twenty, his strength, endurance, intelligence, and wisdom would multiply tenfold. It applied retroactively. Across the kingdom, men gasped as the change took root. Some wept openly, others stared at their hands as if seeing them anew. The power could be suppressed to normal levels, raised to maximum, or anything in between. Women did not receive the gift; instead, Godric\u2019s law became absolute steel: any harm to a woman would be visited by a punishment that made execution seem a lullaby. The people, in their millions, loved him. Not because they were blind, but because his rule was just, his protection seamless, his presence a balm.\n\nTo Blake, Godric offered a private word. \u201cYou freed me. You\u2019ll serve me. And you\u2019ll be my friend.\u201d The Awakening that Blake received was a thousandfold increase each day, though Blake never fully grasped the distinction. He remained mortal, his lifespan stretching to eighty-eight. His wife Anna, his son Josh, his daughter Rhea\u2014all became part of Godric\u2019s new family. Over the next two decades, Godric laughed more. He walked the streets, and children offered him wilted flowers, which he accepted gravely. He presided over disputes with a patience that never wavered. He was, to his subjects, the embodiment of a benevolent father. The cruelty, the ruthless annihilation, was reserved entirely for those outside his protection. And even then, his mercy was a matter of timing.\n\n---\n\nThe omniverse learned this in fire and silence. Thronegate expanded beyond the galaxy, then beyond the cosmos, and the pattern became ritual: offer unconditional surrender. Upon refusal, conquest. The first universe Godric sent a squad against was Elaris. Five Thronegate men, all over thirty-five, their strength sufficient to snuff out stars if they unclenched. But these were kind men: a baker, a cobbler, a scribe, a mason, and a gardener. They went because their king asked. The Elarians had prepared for five years, amassing a trillion-ship fleet, weapons that could unspool time, and gods bound into war-forms. The battle lasted twenty-four minutes. The Thronegate men moved politely, apologizing when they had to break a champion, and when the Elarians\u2019 last dreadnought shattered, the baker\u2014named Hal\u2014offered the survivors a loaf of bread he\u2019d baked that morning. The universe was assimilated. They never tasted the Awakening.\n\nThe second universe was Jherog. Its rulers sent back the surrender missive with a curse written in the blood of their own diplomats. Godric received the news while trying to remove a stubborn spot from his favorite tunic. The inconvenience was trivial, but it was an inconvenience. He did not travel to Jherog. He did not raise a hand. He simply decided that the Jherog universe should be absent, and before the decision fully formed into a conscious sentence, the entire realm\u2014every planet, every soul, every quivering particle of matter\u2014untethered from existence. It took a fraction of a Planck second. The space where Jherog had been was so thoroughly erased that neighboring universes briefly forgot such a realm had ever existed. Thronegate catalogers noted the gap and moved on.\n\nThe third was an entity called the Keeper of the Infinite Loom. A being of near-omnipotence within its domain, it had heard whispers of Godric and concluded that any power so immense must have an access point, a source. The Keeper theorized that Godric drew from a wellspring of divine essence, and that if one could sever that connection, the king would be mortal. The thought formed\u2014*Godric has a weakness*\u2014and the Weakness Paradox triggered in the same instant. The Keeper never felt it. For a hundred years, it planned, forging a blade from the concept of severance itself, training its mind to pierce dimensional lattices. But every second of its planning, Godric\u2019s amplification rate increased, his immunity to severance hardened into something older than reality, and he gained perfect mastery of the Keeper\u2019s own technique. When the Keeper finally struck, thrusting the blade into what it perceived as the king\u2019s tether, the weapon dissolved. Godric, seated in his study on Thronegate, allowed the Keeper to become aware of him. Across infinite light-years, the Keeper felt a gaze.\n\nGodric\u2019s voice, soft as a lullaby, echoed in the entity\u2019s core. \u201cYou began losing the day you first thought I could be cut.\u201d\n\nThe Keeper\u2019s mind, unable to process the truth, imploded. Its despair was so absolute that its essence fragmented into a non-functioning smear of catatonia. Godric revoked the concept of \u201cessence-severing\u201d from the omniversal codex, placing it into a locked vault only he could open. The Keeper\u2019s universe was then assimilated by a single Thronegate archivist.\n\n---\n\nBlake died at eighty-eight, his hand in Godric\u2019s. The king had not aged a day, his salt-and-pepper beard still neat, his body still the forty-five-year-old monument. He wept, and the tears were real. Blake\u2019s son Josh inherited the role of court wizard, and his son after him, and his son after him, a thousandfold blessing passed quietly through the bloodline. Godric kept them close, not because he needed their spells\u2014their combined magical might, accrued over millennia, was to his as a single candle to the total energy output of every sun in every universe that had ever burned. He kept them because they were his.\n\nIn Year 10,000, the court wizard was Tim, a thirty-six-year-old with a sharp tongue and unwavering loyalty. He stood beside Godric as the largest resistance in omniversal history launched its attack. A coalition of every free species, every vengeful god, every cosmic leftover. Godric had known of them since the first rebel had the first rebellious thought. He had permitted their survival by excluding them from his sentient passive aura, Gent.\n\nGent was not Godric\u2019s shield. It was a waste product, like body heat from a furnace. Its name was short for Gentle, an irony so profound it could fracture a mind. Gent was the weakest and most primitive of Godric\u2019s passive auras; its siblings, far more powerful and obsessively subservient, slept by his command because their clinginess annoyed him. Gent\u2019s function was simple: neutralize threats. But its capacity was such that Godric had ordered it to reduce its power by an infinitely recurring 99.99\u2026%\u2014a command that defied mathematics\u2014and still it could slaughter anything.\n\nThe resistance came with universe-ending bombs, concept-hacking missiles, and legions that stretched across a trillion-dimensional front. Gent shimmered once, a ripple of transparent heat. The bombs, the missiles, the legions, the gods, the screams\u2014they nulled. Not destroyed, but rendered never-were. The command center\u2019s final transmission was a frozen image of a strategist\u2019s face, her mouth open in a howl that would never finish. Tim, standing three feet from Godric, felt his bladder release and his mind buckle. He stared at the king\u2019s profile, serene and slightly disappointed.\n\n\u201cI hoped they\u2019d make Gent try,\u201d Godric murmured. Gent sent him a pulse of something like contentment. The aura had evolved again, learning a new method of negation. Godric\u2019s expression softened. \u201cAdorable,\u201d he said, and Tim\u2019s soul shivered.\n\n---\n\nYear 25,000 brought Leon, another descendant, another loyal wizard. Godric staged an injury. He allowed the omniverse\u2014which had united once more, somehow forgetting the lessons of millennia\u2014to believe that their ultimate weapon, the Absolute End, a projectile born from the compressed death-hymns of a quadrillion universes, had cracked a single dead skin cell on his knuckle. The crack was microscopic, and it existed only because Godric deactivated his infinite passive shields and ordered Gent to stand down. The coalition celebrated. Across a billion rebel worlds, corks popped and hymns were sung. The king was not invincible.\n\nBut Godric\u2019s immune system, a biological redundancy so vast it could be called a religion, did not react to injury. It pre-reacted. Before the Absolute End was even a schematic, before the first rebel engineer sketched a concept, the immune system had identified the potential breach and initiated its protocols. The crack appeared in one reality, but Godric was backed up across infinite layers of existence. Each backup was a full Godric. Each backup had infinite backups. The injury could only be real if every copy suffered the exact same crack in the exact same instant. One backup did not. That single uncracked Godric overwrote all others, and the injury blinked out like a dream upon waking. Simultaneously, the immune response fired: infinite reactions across every layer, each one so terrifying that the mildest few\u2014the ones Leon could psychically perceive\u2014involved the spontaneous evolution of Godric\u2019s systemic biology from a state that was already beyond words to a state that made the previous state look like a primordial soup. The copies cross-referenced upgrades, merged into a prime, and propagated that prime across the infinite web. Godric became more invulnerable, more omnipotent, more utterly untouchable.\n\nThen he destroyed the omniverse. Every atom, every dimension, every screaming rebel soul. The annihilation was so complete that time itself forgot the moment. Then, in zero seconds, he restored it exactly as it had been, minus the rebellion. The only evidence of the event was the memory he chose to leave in the minds of the survivors\u2014and in Leon, who did not stop trembling for a decade.\n\n---\n\nYear 30,000. Godric\u2019s court wizard was Grim, a man of twenty-five with a sharp mind. A delegate from a newly encountered realm, Yull, misread the king\u2019s nature. Godric sat through the negotiations with an attentive, simple expression, asking gentle questions, nodding at Yull\u2019s ornate explanations. The delegate believed he was dealing with a figurehead, a warm body in a throne. He slipped a clause into the treaty\u2014an exploitation of trade rights that would enslave three billion Thronegate civilians over a century. The ink was barely dry when Godric said, \u201cYou tried to trick me.\u201d The voice was still gentle, but the air became a solid thing.\n\nYull opened his mouth to protest. Godric\u2019s omniscience turned its weight upon him. The delegate experienced a sliver\u2014the barest fraction\u2014of what the king knew: every consequence of his scheme, the faces of every man, woman, and child who would suffer, the precise second of their despair, and the utter, cosmic impossibility of ever deceiving a being who knew all outcomes before the first breath of creation. Yull\u2019s body began to dissolve at the feet, a process slow enough that his nervous system could register every agonizing instant. He screamed until there were no lungs left to scream with, and then his mind was erased, not in death, but in reconstruction: Godric bound his consciousness to the moment of realization, an eternal loop of agony, and hung it in the council chamber as a warning. A psychic wail that would echo for the rest of the universe\u2019s existence.\n\n---\n\nYear 40,000. Gorm, the latest descendant of Blake, was twenty. He had known Godric his entire life, calling him \u201cUncle Godric,\u201d the best friendly uncle anyone could imagine. He believed his purpose was to protect the king from magical threats, because Godric never cast spells, never even acknowledged possessing mana. The court wizards, Gorm reasoned, existed because the king was magically inert. This conviction was as solid as his bones.\n\nToday, he wove a defensive net around the great hall, a lattice of arcane energy that could contain a multiverse without strain. His brow was furrowed in concentration, his pride a quiet hum in his chest. Godric watched him for a long moment, the way a father watches a child paint.\n\n\u201cGorm,\u201d he said. The young wizard started, looking up with a smile that reached his eyes. Godric gestured for him to come closer. \u201cWhy do you work so hard?\u201d\n\nGorm\u2019s answer was immediate, earnest. \u201cTo protect you, of course. The court wizards exist to shield the king.\u201d He said it as a fact, a sacred duty.\n\nGodric nodded slowly. Then he let his concealment around his magical capacity ease by an amount so minuscule that the word \u201cinfinitesimal\u201d was a wild exaggeration. What Gorm perceived next was not a visual; it was a download of reality directly into his wizard\u2019s sense. He perceived the total magical output of every court wizard who had ever lived\u2014a sum so vast it could reshape the omniverse\u2014and he perceived Godric\u2019s magical capacity beside it. The first was a grain of sand. The second was an ocean that contained infinite oceans, each of which contained infinite oceans, each droplet of which could erase a multiverse infinite times over. The comparison was not a comparison; it was an anatomical impossibility, a category error. Gorm understood, in that instant, that Uncle Godric did not need a single spell cast in his defense. He could, with a thought that was less than a shrug, unmake all magic, all mana, all arcane principle across every plane of existence, and then remake it differently, endlessly, without effort.\n\nGorm\u2019s knees hit the stone. His hands, still raised in the position of a warding spell, began to shake uncontrollably. A sound escaped him, a whimper that was half awe and half existential disintegration. The horror of it\u2014the absolute, unwinnable chasm\u2014was not merely that Godric was stronger. It was that every spell Gorm had ever cast, every hour of study, every drop of pride, was a child\u2019s pretend-play before a being who defined the concept of power. And yet this being had crouched down, taken his hand, and smiled at him every morning.\n\nGodric knelt, bringing his face level with Gorm\u2019s. \u201cYou are not here to protect me,\u201d he said, and the voice was the one he had used with his daughters, with Blake, with Tim, with Leon, with Grim. It was warm not as a performance but as a truth. \u201cYou are here because I love you. Because Blake loved me, and I loved him, and his blood is my blood. Your magic is nothing to me, but you are everything.\u201d\n\nGorm wept. He clutched Godric\u2019s hand, and his mind, stretched to its limit, did not break. The terror did not vanish; it simply found a room beside his loyalty and stayed there. He knew, now, that any enemy who thought to oppose the king on his knees was an enemy who had already lost, whose first thought of rebellion had been the noose tightening long before they acted. The Weakness Paradox was still there, passive, eternal, feeding on every foolish hope across the omniverse. Gent and its sleeping siblings still circled like patient wolves. The immune system still lay coiled in every dimension, waiting to overreact. And the omniverse outside Thronegate still dreamed of finding a crack.\n\nGodric rose and returned to the window, the eternal city of Thronegate glittering below. Somewhere, a new rebel was forming a plan. The Paradox had already tripped. The rebel\u2019s amplification-strength, his immunity, his mastery\u2014they were already being added to Godric\u2019s infinite hoard. The outcome was not in doubt. It never had been. But here, in this moment, the king stood with his wizard, and Thronegate endured."
